# MapSimulator Client Parity Backlog

## Purpose

This document is the single source of truth for MapSimulator parity work against the MapleStory client.

It does three things that the old notes did not do well:

1. Separates shipped work from missing work.
2. Distinguishes broad simulator features from player/avatar parity.
3. Anchors claims to actual code seams and, where relevant, client-side reverse engineering.

## Evidence Used

Notes:
Direct IDA seam capture is now confirmed for inventory, cash-service, item-maker, item-upgrade, map-transfer, equipment, quest-log, quest-detail, quest-alarm, the dedicated ranking/event owners (`CUIRanking`, `CUIEventAlarm`), status-bar utility clicks, stat-window, the explicit key-config/game-option/soft-keyboard owner family (`CUIKeyConfig`, `CUIGameOpt`, `CSoftKeyboardDlg`, `CUIMacroSysEx`, `CUISoftKeyboard`), user-info owners, the book/collection owner family (`CBookDlg` plus `CMonsterBookMan::LoadBook`), the parcel/mail owner family (`CParcelDlg`), the storage/trunk dialog owner (`CTrunkDlg::OnCreate`), the separate service-stage owners for Cash Shop and ITC (`CCashShop`, `CITC`), the stage-internal Cash Shop owners (`CCSWnd_Char`, `CCSWnd_Locker`, `CCSWnd_Inventory`, `CCSWnd_List`, `CCSWnd_Status`, `CCSWnd_OneADay`, `CCashTradingRoomDlg`), the separate cash-service wishlist owner (`CUIAdminShopWishList`), its follow-up search-result/category child owners (`CUIAdminShopWishListSearchResult`, `CUIAdminShopWishListCategory`), the anti-macro challenge owners (`CUIAntiMacro`, `CUIAdminAntiMacro`), the packet-owned anti-macro result bridge in `CWvsContext`, and a broader local-user packet dispatcher for utility/event surfaces. `CUserLocal::OnPacket` is important because it shows the client does not only open these windows from direct button clicks: packet-owned handlers also drive generic `UI_Open`, optioned UI launch, commodity-shop migration, field fade overlays, balloon messages, and damage-meter timer resets. The Cash Shop and ITC decompiles also show that those services are not just alternate button skins on top of `CAdminShopDlg`: `CCashShop::Init` and `CITC::Init` each clear field UI, build their own staged child-window layout, select service BGM, and then wait on service-specific packet dispatch through `OnPacket`. Follow-up decompiles now also show that the stage owners do not directly absorb all of the in-service interaction either: `CCSWnd_Char::OnCreate` builds a dedicated avatar-preview surface with default-avatar, buy-avatar, and takeoff-avatar buttons plus a `CUserPreview`/physics-space pair, `CUIAdminShopWishList::OnCreate` builds a distinct wishlist owner with its own layer, controls, and focused search edit instead of leaving wish-list behavior inside the base shop dialog, the follow-up wishlist scan confirms that search results and category selection also live in dedicated child owners instead of staying anonymous popups, `CCashTradingRoomDlg::OnCreate` builds its own chat edit, buttons, scrollbar, fonts, and cash-balance state inside the service stage, `CUIAntiMacro::{OnCreate,Draw,Update}` confirm a separate timed text-entry owner rather than treating lie-detector checks as item-use restriction text only, `CTrunkDlg::OnCreate` likewise confirms the storage surface as a dedicated dialog owner with its own tabs, buttons, dual-scrollbar layout, and font/title setup before packet-fed state arrives, and `CWvsContext::OnAntiMacroResult` shows that the owner is itself packet-driven rather than purely item- or dialog-launched. The remaining seam-collection gap in this backlog area is now narrower and centered on deeper packet/data ownership inside the newly confirmed utility-owner families plus the still-missing quest reward/revive and adjacent utility-owner follow-through, rather than on the already-captured minimap or explicit skill-macro owner seams.

## Cross-Document Scope Notes

- `CStage::OnSetCashShop` and `CStage::OnSetITC` are login-to-service handoff references that may appear in backlog 11, but the actual Cash Shop / ITC stage ownership belongs here under the external cash-service family.
- `CParcelDlg` and `CTrunkDlg` stay owned by this document, including packet-driven state, draw ownership, and dialog lifecycle. Backlog 10 should only keep the remaining social-system packet owners that are not parcel/trunk utility windows.
- `CCSWnd_Char::ShowPersonalShop` at `0x4bc660`, `CCSWnd_Char::ShowEntrustedShop` at `0x4bc6b0`, and `CCashTradingRoomDlg::OnCreate` at `0x49e8c0` stay owned here as cash-service stage preview/child-window seams. Backlog 10 should track the actual in-field social-room owners (`CPersonalShopDlg`, `CEntrustedShopDlg`, and `CTradingRoomDlg`) rather than duplicating those cash-stage hooks.

## Client Function Index By Backlog Area

The list below maps this backlog area to the concrete client seams that are already named in code or prior reverse-engineering notes.
These are the first functions or classes to inspect before changing simulator behavior.
Packet/controller rows and window/dialog-owner rows are intentionally kept separate when the client splits those responsibilities across different seams, and the index keeps follow-up scan additions close to their first discovery notes.

### 1. Progression and utility window parity

- `CUIStat::Draw`
- `CUIStat::DrawTextA`
- `CUIItem::Draw` at `0x7ccf50`
- `CAdminShopDlg::OnCreate` at `0x42ecd0`

- `CAdminShopDlg::SetAdminShopDlg` at `0x4307c0`

- `CCashShop::Init` at `0x484920`

- `CUISoftKeyboard::UpdateKeyConstraint` at `0x85fd70`
- `CUIUserInfo::Draw` at `0x8b3a50`
- `CUIUserInfo::OnButtonClicked` at `0x8b6d80`
- `CUIEventAlarm::OnCreate` at `0x7ac4f0`
- `CUIEventAlarm::Draw` at `0x7aad90`
- `CUIEventAlarm::Update` at `0x7aac00`

- `CBookDlg::OnButtonClicked` at `0x474300`

- `CTrunkDlg::OnCreate` at `0x768c00`
- `CITC::Init` at `0x573ee0`
- `CITC::OnPacket` at `0x577470`
- `CITC::OnNormalItemResult` at `0x5771d0`
- `CRepairDurabilityDlg` (constructed from `CUserLocal::OnOpenUIWithOption` at `0x932300` when `uiId == 33`)

Notes:
`CUIItem::Draw` confirms that the client inventory window owns meso text, per-slot icon and quantity drawing, item-grade frames, disabled-slot overlays, and special overlays such as the active bullet marker. `CAdminShopDlg::{OnCreate,OnPacket,SetAdminShopDlg,Draw,OnButtonClicked}` now make the cash-service dialog boundary much clearer than the older notes did: the client keeps a dedicated in-map admin-shop owner, and `CField::OnPacket` routes packet types `366` and `367` into that dialog's open/result/reopen lifecycle instead of leaving it as only a status-bar launch plus local button handling. That packet-owned dialog seam is intentionally distinct from the separate `CCashShop` / `CITC` stage owners tracked below. `CUIItemMaker::Draw` and `CUIItemMaker::OnButtonClicked` confirm a dedicated crafting or maker window rather than burying production flow inside generic inventory handling. `CUIItemUpgrade::Draw` and `CUIItemUpgrade::OnButtonClicked` confirm a separate item-enhancement surface rather than treating scroll or upgrade flow as a generic inventory tooltip action. Follow-up IDA lookup now shows Vega enhancement is also a distinct owner rather than a cosmetic branch inside ordinary upgrade flow: `CUIVega::{OnCreate,Draw,OnButtonClicked}` build their own dialog, validate equip/scroll state, gate the cast behind the same exclusive-request checks as the client, and trigger the dedicated Vega effect path after sending the upgrade packet. `CUIMapTransfer::Draw` and `CUIMapTransfer::OnButtonClicked` confirm a dedicated map-transfer window distinct from the minimap shell. `CUIEquip::Draw` confirms that equip-window parity is tied to slot-disable rules, expiration and durability overlays, and job or subjob gating rather than just slot placement. `CUIQuestInfo::Draw`, `CUIQuestInfoDetail::Draw`, and `CUIQuestAlarm::Draw` confirm that quest progression parity includes a separate detail pane with dedicated button handling, category-button rebuilds, scroll-driven list rebuilding, quest-delivery requirement rendering, condition-state coloring, and a standalone quest-alert window rather than only the quest log shell. Follow-up direct lookups now also confirm that the `BtRank` and `BtEvent` status-bar launches land on dedicated client owners rather than unnamed utility shells: `CUIRanking::{OnCreate,OnButtonClicked,Update}` and `CUIEventAlarm::{OnCreate,Draw,Update}`. `CBookDlg::{OnCreate,Draw,OnButtonClicked}` together with `CMonsterBookMan::LoadBook` confirm that the client keeps a real book-style collection owner tied to Monster Book data rather than treating book presentation as a generic stats subpage. `CParcelDlg::{OnCreate,Draw,OnButtonClicked}` confirm a dedicated parcel/mail owner with receive, send, and quick-send surfaces rather than burying package delivery under memo/social text alone. `CUserLocal::OnOpenUIWithOption` now also gives direct client evidence that repair-durability is its own utility owner rather than a generic option toggle: the decompile at `0x932300` shows `uiId == 33` allocating `CRepairDurabilityDlg(v5)` when no `CUniqueModeless` owner is already active. `CUIStatusBar::OnButtonClicked` confirms the utility-button cluster is a real interaction owner instead of only decorative art. `CUIMacroSysEx::OnCreate` together with `CUISoftKeyboard::GetKeyIndexFromPoint`, `CUISoftKeyboard::OnMouseMove`, `CUISoftKeyboard::HitTest`, and `CUISoftKeyboard::UpdateKeyConstraint` confirms that client text-entry parity is not just committed character handling: the macro family also owns an explicit soft-keyboard helper with hover, hit-test, and per-mode key-constraint behavior. `CUIUserInfo::Draw` and `CUIUserInfo::OnButtonClicked` confirm a separate character-information or profile surface beyond the stat window itself.

### 2. Local utility and event packet parity

- `CUserLocal::OnPacket` at `0x9340c0`
- `CUserLocal::OnOpenUI` at `0x9055f0`
- `CUserLocal::OnOpenUIWithOption` at `0x932300`
- `CUserLocal::OnGoToCommoditySN` at `0x905760`
- `CUserLocal::OnFieldFadeInOut` at `0x905790`
- `CUserLocal::OnBalloonMsg` at `0x91d780`
- `CUserLocal::OnDamageMeter` at `0x905620`

Notes:
`CUserLocal::OnPacket` is a distinct client seam rather than a random collection of callbacks. It dispatches packet-owned local utility behavior including `OnOpenUI`, `OnOpenUIWithOption`, `OnGoToCommoditySN`, field fade in/out, balloon messages, damage-meter timing, chat/notice surfaces, quest-guide and delivery-quest results, buff-zone effects, field HP-dec notices, tutor flows, and several event-sound/minigame-sound owners. The narrower decompiles already show concrete responsibilities that are not represented well by the existing window rows: `OnOpenUI` forwards a raw UI id into `CWvsContext::UI_Open`, `OnOpenUIWithOption` adds option-driven branches such as party-search requests and the repair-durability owner, `OnGoToCommoditySN` stores a commodity serial number before calling `SendMigrateToShopRequest`, `OnFieldFadeInOut` registers a fade animation relative to the avatar layer Z, `OnBalloonMsg` can bind a balloon to the avatar origin or an explicit world position, and `OnDamageMeter` resets a dedicated timer surface. That means the client has a packet-driven utility/event layer that sits between local gameplay and the specific window owners already tracked above.

### 3. Packet-authored local overlays and guidance parity

- `CUserLocal::OnFieldFadeInOut` at `0x905790`
- `CUserLocal::OnBalloonMsg` at `0x91d780`
- `CUserLocal::OnDamageMeter` at `0x905620`
- `CUserLocal::OnNotifyHPDecByField` at `0x90fed0`
- `CUserLocal::OnQuestGuideResult` at `0x90f1e0`
- `CUserLocal::OnDeliveryQuest` at `0x90ef60`
- `CUserLocal::OnOpenClassCompetitionPage` at `0x905580`

Notes:
These handlers form a narrower client-owned feedback layer under `CUserLocal::OnPacket`, and the current backlog only references them inside the broad dispatcher row. IDA now confirms concrete responsibilities that deserve separate tracking: `OnFieldFadeInOut` decodes fade-in, fade-out, and duration fields then registers the animation relative to the avatar layer Z; `OnBalloonMsg` decodes text, width, lifetime, and either avatar-relative or explicit world-position placement before calling `ShowBallonMsg`; `OnDamageMeter` resets the dedicated damage-meter timer owner and updates shared timing state in `CWvsContext`; `OnQuestGuideResult` rebuilds quest-demand targets and opens the world-map quest-guide owner when the packet contains viable quest-mob targets; `OnDeliveryQuest` either opens the dedicated delivery-quest owner or routes the result back through the status-bar chat seam when another unique modeless owner is active; and `OnOpenClassCompetitionPage` is a packet-driven utility launch rather than a normal button path.

### 4. External cash-service stage parity

- `CCashShop::Init` at `0x484920`
- `CCashShop::OnPacket` at `0x4997e0`
- `CCashShop::OnCashItemResult` at `0x499370`
- `CITC::Init` at `0x573ee0`
- `CITC::OnPacket` at `0x577470`
- `CITC::OnNormalItemResult` at `0x5771d0`

Notes:
This service-stage surface is distinct from the in-map `CAdminShopDlg` approximation already tracked above. IDA shows `CCashShop::Init` and `CITC::Init` clearing field UI, constructing their own staged child-window layouts, selecting service BGM, and entering standalone stage owners rather than opening one more utility dialog over the live HUD. The packet routers are distinct too: `CCashShop::OnPacket` dispatches cash-service result families such as charge-param, query-cash, cash-item, purchase-exp, gift-mate, duplicate-id, name-change, transfer-world, gachapon, one-a-day, and free-item notices, while `CITC::OnPacket` owns its own smaller result family around charge-param, query-cash, and normal-item results. That means Cash Shop and ITC parity should be tracked as their own service-stage owner family rather than being treated as a subset of status-bar launches or the current admin-shop fallback.

### 5. Cash-service child-window and preview parity discovered by targeted IDA scan

- `CCSWnd_Char::BlowWeather` at `0x4c5d30`

- `CCSWnd_Status::OnCreate` at `0x4cb840`

Separate owners then build the rest of the service UI: `CCSWnd_Locker`, `CCSWnd_Inventory`, `CCSWnd_List`, and `CCSWnd_Status` each have their own `OnCreate` routines, `CCSWnd_OneADay::OnCreate` owns the One-a-Day panel inside the service, and `CCashTradingRoomDlg::OnCreate` builds a standalone cash trading room with its own chat edit, trade/coin buttons, scrollbar, fonts, and initial cash balance. None of these client-owned child-window seams are named anywhere else in the backlog today even though they sit directly on the parity path for cash-avatar preview and service-stage usability.

### 7. Packet-authored radio-schedule parity discovered by targeted IDA scan

- `CUserLocal::OnRadioSchedule` at `0x918120`
- `CRadioManager::Play` at `0x6cb940`
- `CRadioManager::Stop` at `0x6cbd20`
- `CRadioManager::Update` at `0x6cbf20`

Notes:
The broader local-utility row already mentioned tutor/radio handlers as a residual gap, but targeted IDA lookup shows radio scheduling is its own client-owned lifecycle rather than one more generic sound callback. `CUserLocal::OnRadioSchedule` decodes a track name plus time value and forwards that payload into a singleton `CRadioManager` owner when no radio session is already active. `CRadioManager::Play` then resolves a WZ/UOL-backed track through `StringPool`, starts multimedia playback, stores the active track name, mutes field BGM through the sound manager, shows a dedicated radio UI, and pushes a chat-log notice for the start event; `CRadioManager::Stop` reverses that ownership by stopping playback, hiding the UI, restoring BGM state, and pushing the completion notice; and `CRadioManager::Update` confirms a timer-driven runtime instead of a fire-and-forget sound effect.

- Area: `Radio schedule and CRadioManager lifecycle parity`
- Current status: `Partial`
- Gap summary: `MapSimulator.PacketOwnedUtilityParity.cs` still keeps the client-shaped `CRadioManager` owner behavior inside the existing radio seam, still mirrors the recovered `StringPool` lookup order by resolving `StringPool[0x1501] = "Sound/Radio.img/%s"` before `StringPool[0x1502] = "Sound/Radio.img/%s/track"` so track-metadata lookup stays distinct from playable sound lookup, still blocks re-entry while a session is live, still clears the live track/audio descriptors together with the playback state on stop, and still seeds its expected stop from remaining runtime (`ms_length - ms_position`) before polling completion on the client-shaped `~2000 ms` cadence. This pass narrows the last simulator shortcuts in that seam without widening ownership elsewhere: the radio owner now refuses the old simulator-only fallback that treated the `StringPool[0x1501]` metadata node as playable audio when the client-authored `StringPool[0x1502]` `/track` sound lookup is absent, and the track title now mirrors `CRadioManager::Play` more closely by preferring the recovered track-property `name` field before descriptor fallback, and create-layer context resets now persist per-character mutation state immediately after runtime character transitions. `MapleStoryStringPool` still carries the recovered radio-owner literals (`0x14CF`, `0x14D0`, `0x1501`, `0x1502`), and `UnitTest_MapSimulator/PacketOwnedRadioParityTests.cs` now locks the exact client track/audio descriptor templates, the lowercase-`name` display-name resolution, the expected-stop / first-poll timing, and the recovered radio string-pool entries so the radio path-shape and owner wording do not drift again. WZ was rechecked again in the active extracted data source: `UI/UIWindow.img/Radio/Off/0` is still `54x32`, `UI/UIWindow.img/Radio/On/0-4` are still `54x32`, and each animated `On` frame still carries `delay = 150`. The remaining gap is narrower and stays concentrated in true client-owned playback and packet authorship: playback still terminates through the MonoGame/WZ backend instead of the client's `CRadioManager::MMS_Play` `IWzSound -> raw buffer -> AIL_quick_load_mem / AIL_quick_set_ms_position / AIL_quick_play` handle path, `CRadioManager::Stop`/`Update` are still simulated around that backend rather than the real AIL handle state, and `CWvsContext[3562]` is still simulator-owned context state rather than an official packet-fed client slot.`

### 9. Tutor, skill-guide, and AP/SP helper parity discovered by `CUserLocal::OnPacket` scan

- `CUserLocal::OnHireTutor` at `0x90e560`

- `CUserLocal::OnOpenSkillGuide` at `0x90e6a0`
- `CUserLocal::OnAskAPSPEvent` at `0x90f0e0`

Notes:
The broader local-utility row currently mentions tutor flows only as residual dispatch coverage, but the targeted `CUserLocal::OnPacket` decompiles show a distinct client-owned helper surface. `OnHireTutor` tears down the prior tutor owner, allocates a `CTutor`, initializes it through the same summoned-style world seam the client uses, and tracks active tutor variants in `CUserLocal::ms_anTutors`; `OnTutorMsg` then forwards either numeric or string payloads plus two packet-owned ints into `CTutor::OnMessage` instead of using ordinary chat. The same scan also shows that guided helper flows are not only local button opens: `OnOpenSkillGuide` packet-opens the skill UI and immediately calls `CUISkill::OpenCurSkillGuide`, while `OnAskAPSPEvent` opens a Yes/No prompt and can emit a follow-up outpacket (`195`) when the player accepts. None of those owner-specific tutor/helper semantics are tracked explicitly in the backlog today.

That is concrete client evidence for minimap-specific owner logic rather than only simulator-side UI structure.

- Area: `Random Morph dialog and outbound request parity`
- Status: `Implemented`
- Gap: The simulator now registers the dedicated `RandomMorph` owner from `UI/UIWindow.img/Transform`, opens it for mounted WZ consume items that publish `spec/morphRandom` instead of routing those items through the self-morph consumable path, enforces the client owner position/button/edit layout, respects the unique-modeless gate, clears the full `300x131` owner surface before draw, emits opcode `184` with update time, 1-based inventory position, item id, and target name while surfacing the StringPool `0x136` blocked-send notice, and now also routes inbound local-utility packets `123` / `1042` through the same owner seam so the recovered exclusive-request latch is cleared by result or ack traffic rather than only by local timeout. `CWvsContext::OnRandomMorphRes` parity is now mirrored closely enough to refresh the request timestamp on inbound result, show the client notices from StringPool `0x1320` (`Failed to find user %s.`) and `0x1321` (`You can use random transform potion only in the town.`), and leave the row's remaining work outside this dialog/request owner.

## Current State Summary

MapSimulator is no longer "missing player simulation".
The project already has:

- A playable local character with foothold, ladder, rope, swim, fly, jump, prone, hit, death, and respawn states.
- Character WZ loading for body, head, face, hair, equipment, weapon overlays, z-map ordering, and slot-visibility conflicts.
- A working generic skill system with job skill loading, buffs, cooldowns, projectiles, hit effects, and quick-slot assignment.
- Mob and drop pools, hidden portal support, damage number rendering from WZ assets, mob HP bars, and boss HP bars.
- Several field-effect systems and special field implementations that are already present in the current simulator.

The real parity gap is no longer "does the simulator have a feature at all?".
The gap is now "how closely does the current implementation match client behavior, data selection, timing, and fallback rules?".

## Recent Progress Summary

Recent implementation progress has been folded into the backlog tables below instead of being tracked as a separate changelog.
The main baseline updates worth keeping visible are:

- Avatar parity moved out of the stub phase: action coverage, rare-action rendering, facial expression behavior, and anchor fallback rules are implemented, while mount and transform handling is partially in place.
- Skill parity is broader than the old notes implied: the simulator now loads and casts the full player skill catalog, supports runtime job swaps, shows buff and cooldown feedback, and covers more movement-family and summon behavior.
- Physics and movement now have real runtime seams for ladder lookup, float collision, movement-path snapshots, and moving-platform foothold sync.
- Combat and UI both shifted from "missing feature" to "refinement": HP indicators, damage rendering, status-bar layout, warning flashes, chat strip behavior, skill UI layout, and tooltip reuse all exist but still need client-accurate polish.
- NPC and quest interaction now have a usable simulator baseline through dialogue overlays, quest lists, and common quest-state mutations, but full scripting and inventory-backed requirements remain incomplete.
- Progression or utility window groundwork now has a shared seam: named owners for world map, map transfer, cash-service, crafting, enhancement, character-info, and quest-side utility windows are registered with `UIWindowManager`, while minimap and status-bar utility buttons now route into those owners instead of staying entirely dead-ended. The dedicated pre-field `WorldSelect`, `ChannelSelect`, and `ChannelShift` selector family is tracked in backlog 11; this utility-window document only keeps the gameplay-side launch and gating hooks that hand control over to those login-owned selectors. The map-transfer owner now also keeps saved teleport destinations in a character-scoped destination book keyed to the active player or selected login-roster character instead of sharing one global saved list across every simulator avatar, persists that destination book under the simulator AppData profile across restarts, and hands the currently selected transfer target into the world-map owner when `BtMap` is used so the two navigation surfaces stay linked.

## Broad IDA Cross-Check

A broad follow-up `list_functions` sweep against the v95 client, compared back against the full backlog corpus, still did not surface another owner family that needs a new split document, but it did expose one smaller cash-service modal-dialog family that belongs in this document. A subsequent targeted `CWvsContext::OnPacket` pass also exposed two smaller context-owned utility owners that belong here.

The candidates that initially looked like possible omissions are already represented by existing rows instead of needing a new split document or duplicate utility section:

- `CWorldMapDlg` / `CreateWorldMapDlg` remain covered by the world-map and minimap-owner rows in this backlog.
- `CSlideMenuDlg` remains covered by the packet-script/message row in backlog 7, where the client owns it through `OnAskSlideMenu`.
- `CConnectionNoticeDlg`, `CPinCodeDlg`, and `CConfirmRaceDlg` remain covered by the login and character-entry backlog in document 11.
- `CWeddingWishListDlg` plus `CWishListRecvDlg`, `CWishListGiveDlg`, and `CWishListInputDlg` remain covered by the companion/social backlog in document 10.
- `CAdminShopDlg`, `CBookDlg`, `CStoreBankDlg`, `CGuildRankDlg`, and the other high-signal utility/social families surfaced by the scan are already named inside this backlog or the dedicated social backlog instead of being truly absent.

That means the right follow-up from this scan is to keep extending the existing rows above, not to add another umbrella utility backlog section that would duplicate ownership across documents. The one new utility-area split that did survive the cross-check is the cash-service modal-dialog family added below, because those owners were still absent from every backlog document rather than merely hidden under an existing row title.

Please turn up the volume."`, `StringPool[0x14D0] = "[%s]'s broadcasting has ended."`, `StringPool[0x1501] = "Sound/Radio.img/%s"`, and `StringPool[0x1502] = "Sound/Radio.img/%s/track"`. The dedicated `RadioStatusWindow` owner and tooltip diagnostics expose the recovered `CUIRadio::CreateLayer` seam by preferring the packet-owned `CWvsContext[3562]` override when present but otherwise falling back to the live minimap expanded-state branch for `bLeft`, still applying `nMargin = 40`, `Origin_RT`, and the concrete `UI/UIWindow.img/Radio/{On,Off}` art, and freezing the active HUD to the session's captured `CreateLayer` side instead of re-evaluating minimap expansion every draw. `PacketOwnedLocalUtilityContextState` keeps a dedicated per-character radio slot lifecycle for `CWvsContext[3562]`, including runtime binding, character-transition reset, mutation sequence tracking, persisted reset mutations, and last-mutation diagnostics. The radio-owner mute lifecycle now follows the recovered owner stack more closely: a successful packet Play unmutes the radio owner, the utility audio mix suppresses field BGM while radio playback owns the live session, Stop remutes the radio owner and restores the BGM target, and the radio HUD indicator/fade is driven from `_packetOwnedRadioMuted` instead of the unrelated utility-BGM mute state. `UnitTest_MapSimulator/PacketOwnedRadioParityTests.cs` and `UnitTest_MapSimulator/PacketOwnedUtilityParityTests.cs` lock the playback-window math, expected-stop timing, offset rejection, formatted start/path diagnostics, `bLeft` resolution order, packet-owned `CWvsContext[3562]` mutation history, and radio-owner audio mix targets. WZ was rechecked in `E:\MapleStory\WzExport\v95_2`: `UI/UIWindow.img/Radio/Off/0` still carries the `54x32` anchor canvas, while `UI/UIWindow.img/Radio/On/0-4` still carry `54x32` animated frames with `delay = 150` on each child. Remaining parity is concentrated in the client-owned playback stack and true packet authorship: playback still terminates through the MonoGame/WZ backend instead of the client's `CRadioManager::MMS_Play` `IWzSound -> raw buffer -> AIL_quick_load_mem / AIL_quick_set_ms_position / AIL_quick_play` handle path, exact native handle stop/update state is still approximated by simulator descriptors, and `CWvsContext[3562]` is still simulator-owned context state unless the official-session bridge supplies real packet mutation history. | Packet-owned radio scheduling is more than a sound trigger. It is a client-managed audio/UI/chat lifecycle that temporarily changes BGM ownership and presents user-facing state, so leaving it inside the generic dispatcher row makes the remaining gap look smaller and less coherent than it is. Tracking it explicitly keeps future work anchored to the right packet handler and manager lifecycle instead of folding radio playback into unrelated sound-effect or notice work. | packet-owned radio manager layer (`CUserLocal::OnRadioSchedule`, `CRadioManager::Play`, `CRadioManager::Update`, `CRadioManager::Stop`) |

| Partial | Explicit key-config, game-option, and soft-keyboard owner parity | The simulator now carries this owner family more explicitly instead of only relying on generic utility launches. `KeyConfigWindow` still keeps the client-owned main vs quick-slot page split from `UIWindow2.img/KeyConfig`, stages edits until `OK`, preserves `Cancel`, and keeps the quick-slot settings page as a dedicated owner branch rather than a status-bar stub; the footer seam remains wired into the live `FuncKeyMapped` translation path, and this pass also carries the recovered palette-owner side of that same client path more directly. WZ inspection still anchors the authored footer families to `KeyConfig/icon/*` in deterministic `0`-`32`, `50`-`54`, `100`-`106` order, while the targeted IDA recovery of `CUIKeyConfig::{ResetPaletteItems,GetPaletteSlotFromIdx}` now lets the simulator feed packet-owned function/control/emotion ids back into those exact WZ icon families instead of treating every non-row packet owner as text only. That means the selected-row footer and live row previews can now show recovered palette ownership for packet-owned function/control/emotion entries, while bindable rows still surface live packet-owned `skill`, `item`, `cash item`, and `macro` ownership through the existing hotkey/shortcut visual seam with the same live slot state already staged into the simulator runtime. `OptionMenuWindow` remains aligned with the recovered `CUIGameOpt::OnCreate` roster and staging lifecycle: the simulator-side checkbox list already matches the recovered `1001`-`1014` client ids, y positions, and ordering, still snapshots current game/system/extra/joypad values on show, and still commits only on `OK` while `Cancel` drops the staged owner state. The soft-keyboard path also remains close to the explicit `CSoftKeyboardDlg` family instead of stopping at helper hit-testing: `SoftKeyboardUI` still loads the full per-key `SoftKeyboard/key/*` families plus `funckey/{capslock,lshift,rshift,enter,backspace}`, randomizes the numeric row per owner session and again when the numeric tab is reselected, keeps the recovered three-tab owner header and compact-vs-expanded layout, follows the switching-character branch by latching active T9 groups, cycling same-group presses through the client-style `1010`-`1018` / `1020`-`1028` letter families, clearing that state on tab or case changes, and now clears stale switching ownership not only on idle timeout or length drift but also when the live host text itself diverges from the staged switching snapshot. The host-side edit owners that already implement `ISoftKeyboardHost` now expose their current text through the shared seam so `SoftKeyboardUI` can detect that divergence directly instead of inferring it only from text length. `UIWindowManager` still reasserts modal owner focus after handled soft-keyboard button clicks instead of only restoring that ownership when the keyboard closes or its host disappears, which keeps the simulator close to the `CSoftKeyboardDlg::OnButtonClicked` branch that repeatedly pushes focus back onto the active edit owner. The remaining gap is now narrower and specific: the simulator still does not reproduce the ### 9. Tutor, skill-guide, and AP/SP helper parity discovered by `CUserLocal::OnPacket` scan

| Status | Area | Gap | Why it matters | Primary seam |
|--------|------|-----|----------------|--------------|
| Partial | Tutor summon and message parity | The simulator keeps tutor traffic on a dedicated packet-owned runtime and summoned-owner seam: local client packets `255`/`256` drive hire/message, resolve the Cygnus (`10001013`) vs Aran (`20001013`) variant from the local job family, use the WZ-backed summoned heights from `Skill/1000.img/skill/10001013/summon/height = 80` and `Skill/2000.img/skill/20001013/summon/height = 70`, render text through the WZ-authored `UI/ChatBalloon.img/tutorial` skin, render indexed cues through `UI/tutorial.img/<index>` with the client-style half-width and `(layerHeight + summonHeight)` placement, and trigger tutor `say` playback through the summoned seam including the recovered Aran numeric-cue exception. Runtime/shared tutor bookkeeping now carries the client-style ordered tutor slot list, static shared active-variant/message snapshots, remove-before-hire lifecycle, local rebind restoration, shared visible actor/message display, owner-specific synthesized summon ids, and the level-11 `CWvsContext::OnStatChanged -> CUserLocal::RemoveTutor` teardown through the same skill-id removal path. The non-local bridge now keeps tutor opcode learning on captured owner evidence instead of a one-packet shape guess: v95-known local tutor opcodes still map from the recovered `CUserLocal::OnPacket` owner table plus exact remote wrapper validation, unknown official-session builds collect distinct wrapper signatures per build, require paired hire/message tutor-owner proof before promoting build-scoped learned mappings, reject same-opcode hire/message shape conflicts, preserve manual mappings, clear learned tutor mappings on reset/unmap, and now reports first-observation official-session evidence accurately in bridge status. `UnitTest_MapSimulator/RemoteUserTutorOfficialSessionBridgeParityTests.cs` covers unknown-build paired tutor inference, promoted cached hire/message mappings, and single-opcode shape-conflict rejection. Remaining gap: the remote bridge still depends on exact remote-wrapper proof plus the recovered v95 owner table instead of a fully recovered native non-local `CUser` opcode owner table with captured live-session proof for every server build, the simulator still approximates the native `CTutor`/`CSummoned` object and COM-layer choreography through the simulator summoned/runtime seams, and broader adjacent `CWvsContext::OnStatChanged` tutorial side effects around the level-up branch still stop at tutor teardown instead of reproducing every native effect/UI path byte for byte. | Leaving tutor flows buried inside the generic local-utility row hides a separate visible helper actor plus packet-authored message lifecycle that can break tutorial or guided-play fields in ways ordinary notice/chat parity will not catch. Tracking the tutor owner explicitly keeps future parity work anchored to the right packet handlers and actor lifecycle instead of treating tutoring as another dialog string. | packet-owned tutor/helper actor layer (`CUserLocal::OnHireTutor`, `CUserLocal::OnTutorMsg`, `CTutor::OnMessage`, `CWvsContext::OnStatChanged`, summoned-style tutor initialization inside `CUserLocal::OnHireTutor`, local-utility official-session bridge for live opcode `255`/`256` mirroring, remote-user official-session bridge build-scoped exact-wrapper proof for non-local tutor hire/message opcodes, `RemoteUserOfficialSessionBridgeManager`, `UnitTest_MapSimulator/RemoteUserTutorOfficialSessionBridgeParityTests.cs`) |
| Implemented | Packet-authored skill-guide and AP/SP helper prompt parity | The simulator now tracks the dedicated `CUserLocal::OnOpenSkillGuide` dispatch as client packet `262`, exposes a `skillguide` alias on the local utility inbox/command seam, packet-opens the skill owner through the existing `UI_Open(3, 1)` path that matches the IDA seam at `0x90e6a0`, and explicitly opens the current Aran guide page when the active job has one. `CUserLocal::OnAskAPSPEvent` is also modeled beyond plain text now: packet `273`/`1008` decodes the client-shaped two-Int32 payload, validates it against the recovered `CWvsContext+0x20B4` receive token from the IDA seam at `0x90f0e0`, opens the helper prompt with the exact recovered `StringPool::ms_aString[0x17BA]` copy from `MapleStory.exe`, uses `OK` and `Cancel` labels to match that copy, and simulates the accepted follow-up outpacket `195` with response `6` through a separate send-context token path mirroring the client `CWvsContext+0x2030` field split. The AP/SP receive/send tokens now persist under a broader simulator-side packet-owned local utility `CWvsContext` owner instead of an AP/SP-only seam: that owner initializes once for the active character, preserves detached receive/send divergence while that character remains active, and resets only when the simulator actually transitions to another local character so stale prompts and follow-up state do not leak across sessions. | These helper prompts sit between tutorial/script flow and ordinary utility windows. Keeping them explicit prevents the broader local-utility dispatcher row from looking complete once the simulator can only show text or open the guide manually, and it anchors future work to the packet-driven launch/confirm path the client actually uses. | packet-owned helper prompt layer (`CUserLocal::OnOpenSkillGuide`, `CUISkill::OpenCurSkillGuide`, `CUserLocal::OnAskAPSPEvent`) |

### 10. Explicit minimap owner parity discovered by targeted IDA scan

| Status | Area | Gap | Why it matters | Primary seam |
|--------|------|-----|----------------|--------------|
| Partial | Explicit minimap owner parity | `MinimapUI` now mirrors the concrete `CUIMiniMap` owner path more closely instead of only carrying broad simulator-side behavior: the loader consumes the client WZ `UIWindow2.img/MiniMap/MinMap`, `MaxMap`, `Min`, and `BtSmall` assets that were previously ignored, the minimap owner now switches between compact and expanded minimap options through its own button family, preserves the previous expanded option when `BtMin` collapses the window, restores that remembered option on `BtMax`, keeps the world-map launch routed directly into the dedicated `WorldMapUI` owner instead of the separate map-transfer window, and still performs a `CWorldMapDlg::CreateWorldMapDlg`-style preflight before showing the world map with the dedicated failure-notice branch tied to `StringPool[0x118]` when the current field cannot be presented by the simulator world-map owner. ### 16. Packet-owned NPC shop, store-bank, and battle-record owners discovered by follow-up `CField::OnPacket` decompile

| Status | Area | Gap | Why it matters | Primary seam |

| Partial | Packet-owned NPC shop, store-bank, and battle-record parity | `HaCreator/MapSimulator` now has explicit packet-owned `NpcShop`, `StoreBank`, and `BattleRecord` windows backed by the WZ-owned `UIWindow2.img/Shop`, `UIWindow2.img/StoreBank`, and `UIWindow2.img/BattleRecord` seams, plus dedicated runtimes and a focused `/npcutility` command surface for `364`/`365`, `369`/`370`, and `420` through `423`. ## Priority Order

If the goal is visible parity first, the next work in this area should be sequenced like this:

1. Window usefulness pass:
   Finish minimap, inventory, equip, and quest-log interactions so the existing windows become usable client-facing tools rather than frame shells.
2. Progression correctness pass:
   Tighten ability/stat formulas, equip presentation, and inventory-backed validations so the windows reflect the runtime accurately.
3. External cash-service ownership pass:
   Add dedicated Cash Shop and ITC stage owners, and route the in-map `CAdminShopDlg::OnPacket` `366`/`367` lifecycle before treating cash-service parity as an extension of `CAdminShopDlg` shell drawing, `OnGoToCommoditySN`, or the local utility bridge.
4. Cash-service subwindow pass:
   Add the avatar-preview, locker, inventory, list, status, One-a-Day, and cash-trading child owners after the base service stages exist so cash-item preview and service-pane behavior do not stay folded into one coarse stage row.
5. Cash-service modal-dialog pass:
   Add the coupon-selection, purchase-confirmation, receive-gift, name-change-license, and transfer-world-license owners after the base service stages and child panes exist so cash-item result and entitlement flows do not stay flattened into generic notices.
6. Cash-service wishlist pass:
   Add the dedicated `CUIAdminShopWishList`-style owner after the base service stages and child panes exist so wish-list search/toggle behavior does not stay buried inside the coarse admin-shop row.
7. Anti-macro packet/result pass:
   Add the `CWvsContext::OnAntiMacroResult` bridge, screenshot/notice side effects, combo-hold lifecycle, and admin-vs-normal owner split before treating lie-detector parity as covered by an owner shell alone.
8. Anti-macro owner pass:
   Add the dedicated `CUIAntiMacro`-style timed text-entry owner after the packet/result bridge exists so the launch and timeout flow does not stay inferred from item bans or generic notice text.
9. Utility-owner refinement pass:
   Tighten `CUIKeyConfig`, `CUIGameOpt`, and `CSoftKeyboardDlg` lifecycle parity after the broad utility buttons work so key-binding, option, and soft-keyboard behavior does not stay hidden inside the generic cursor/utility row.
10. Macro-owner refinement pass:
   Tighten `CUIMacroSysEx` draw/button-owner parity after the macro surface and shared text-entry seams exist so macro behavior does not stay documented only as input polish.
11. Utility feedback pass:
   Complete pickup notices, soft-keyboard or constrained text-entry behavior, macro behavior, cursor states, and status-bar utility-button behavior.
12. Production/effect animation pass:
   Split maker, upgrade, hammer, skill-book, Vega, and cash-gachapon result-effect ownership out from the window and cash-stage rows before more reward presentation drifts into packet summaries or window-local implementations only.
13. Owner-consolidation pass:
   Refresh older umbrella rows so minimap, macro, inventory, equip, and quest utility work stays anchored to the explicit client owners already captured here instead of drifting back into stale generic-window buckets.

## Working Rule For Future Updates

Update this file directly, and always classify each item as one of:

- `Implemented`
- `Partial`
- `Missing`

That keeps the backlog honest and prevents already-shipped work from reappearing as "missing".
